* and need to figure out a better overall way to interface with prjn-based weights
versus conspec based -- doesn't work right now with sender-based init weights.

* Appropriate enabling of edit menu items also fixed
* The problem was that GetEditActionsEnabled() and other related code wasn't implemented for text fields. The solution was to check to see if the widget in focus was a QLineWidget and if so call the edit method on that widget, otherwise pass the edit on to the datatable, tree, etc.

7484
 
2014-09-02
 
rohrlich
 
* Code added to iLineEdit::focusInEvent to modify table cell editing broke menu behavior (cut/copy didn't work) for
menus in single line text fields. The problem was that the new focus code was deselecting before cut/copy was called
and thus cut/copy didn't see a selection.
* Also, while in that code I added a preference "alt_cell_editing" so that users can have the new style of cell
editing (the alt style) or traditional editing for data table cells.

7486
 
2014-09-02
 
oreilly
 
* unit knows its own unit group index with member ug_idx
* got rid of inhib_mode = LAY_AND_GPS -- now have better macros for HasUnitGpInhib, vs
  HasLayerInhib
* major reorganiziation and simplification of all the Leabra Compute_* functions into
 the minimal set of separate paths through (netin, netin integ, inhib, act, cycle stats)
* separate timing of each of these steps in cyc_threads -- very clear that cons vs.
  units vs. layers all need to be optimized separately.
* surprisingly long wait timing and high run timing for various steps that I would have
  thought shouldn't take that much time -- lots to look at and tune now..

7488
 
2014-09-03
 
oreilly
 
* comment out "keypress" debug stmt from iLineEdit
* cycle-by-cycle tracking of threaded compute costs -- VERY illuminating.  by far the simplest alternative is to just interleave the threads across units -- neighboring units
are most likely to share similar loads.  the cost is cache consistency per processor -- 
but the load balancing wins out in the end.. and the simplicity is a major factor..
* if not doing any decay, then do not reset the netin computation!  this is a HUGE
savings in compute time..
* now getting 2.16 x faster than 7.0.1, with 4 threads.

2014-09-06
 
oreilly
 
* fixed the unit/layer "nibble" loop logic -- counter was NOT getting reset back to 0
in a fully sync'd manner, so sometimes things started in weird places or got started 
twice -- now passing the loop index and alternating sequential steps to avoid
* this fixes a significant computational bug with previous code!!
* also, btw, the recent cifer impl of learning rates was causing lrate creep through
the loop -- by multiplying clrate over and over -- fixed in prior checkin.

7512
 
2014-09-07
 
oreilly
 
* removed old USE_SSE8
* added ta_vector_ops.h header that provides TA_VEC_USE and TA_VEC_SIZE and VECF, VECI 
macros, which auto-size based on the instruction set avail of the compiler -- 7 = 4, =>8 = 8.
* include compile_info as expert member in taMisc / preferences -- can now see what 
the compiler figured out about your architecture (sort of at least based on what defines
are currently processed -- in taMisc::Initialize)
* improved configure script to take --flags= option where you can pass arbitrary flags
* discovered that haswell is not detected with -march=native -- have to pass in -mavx2
* eliminated outdated params from old threading code in various places
* rewrote conspec vec code to use generic VEC macros
* after all this, NO change in performance for using vec8 versus vec4 on haswell laptop..

7515
 
2014-09-07
 
krueger
 
An attempt to isolate the individual test more from each other.

If a program ran too long, then it would keep the server API busy and
all subsequent tests would fail.

Therefore check before each test that the we can get a RunState of done and if not,
kill and restart emergent to have a clean state for the next test.


7516
 
2014-09-08
 
rohrlich
 
If the user has already typed the new variable just query for local/global

7517
 
2014-09-08
 
krueger
 
Emergent segfaults on close.

This is likely caused by a thread synchronization issue causing the cleanup code to run in the wrong order.

I haven't figured out the correct way to solve it, but adding a sleep(1) appears to drastically reduce the frequency
of segfaults on close, so add this hack for now until someone can fix the underlying issue correctly.


7518
 
2014-09-08
 
oreilly
 
* LeabraConSpec now supports (optional) fast weights, which replaces the previous
stable weights mechanism -- fast_wts member has the params -- very simple mech --
very simple tests suggest it seems to not interfere with regular randomized learning too much..
* got rid of previous, non-functional FastWtConSpec 
* no longer saving pdw as a way to view weight changes -- this was rather extravagant
just for the very rare visualization of this value -- now you just have to turn off the
Compute_Weights call to see the dwts..
* fwt (fast weight) and swt (slow weight) are saved as *linear* and not nonlin guys -- this
is a net savings for accuracy and complexity, and needed for basic fast wts mechanism
* fixed prior bug that was causing e.g., LeabraStd.proj to converge slowly (in addition
to the stable wts problem): bad indexing in vector Compute_dWt guys!
* test project for bug BugID:2049 with control panel for now-missing member (stable_mix)
* updated LeabraStd.proj with new default specs -- still need to update programs etc.

7526
 
2014-09-10
 
oreilly
 
* proposed fix for Kai's css startup script bug
* added units_flat.size check to Network thread functions that could be called without a
built network -- maybe prevents John's crash bug in threads??
* MASSIVE surgery to LeabraUnit / LeabraUnitSpec:
:* eliminate old hyst and accom, and  gc.h and gc.a, in favor of new adapt and stp mechanisms
:* all rate constants now entered as time constants in milliseconds, with clearer comments
:* eliminate maxda and associated junk -- this will cause standard Settle prog to break, but fix is easy (just cut out one condition line about maxda)
:* only gelin is supported in main unit spec -- will add a new unit spec to support non-gelin for legacy code -- cleaned up functions with clearer names (ActFun instead of ActFmVm, given that gelin doesn't actually compute act fm vm..)
:* got rid of separate act_lrn activation function -- wasn't useful.
:* got rid of phase_diff_ratio and associated opt param.
:* added spike variable, which is generated for rate-code acts, enabling spike-based adapt and stp to work directly from single spike variable
:* added cascade option to act_avg SRAvg computations -- need to try that out
:* still need to finish stp impl and fix lrates in fast con spec, and add wt adapt rate

7528
 
2014-09-10
 
oreilly
 
Should finally fix John's bug!  the problem was inferring which direction to go based
on start/stop parameters -- if a given thread was very slow in getting started, it would
incorrectly enter the backwards branch, and from there, all hell breaks loose.
now caching the backwards parameter explicitly and using that to unambiguously decide
which way to go..

7533
 
2014-09-11
 
rohrlich
 
Fix for 2049 - controlpanel crashes with no-longer-valid member.
The underlying problem is that the list of widgets doesn't include
the invalid member but the control panel still includes the item in
its member list. Just skipping is sufficient because the lists are out
of sync. I fixed the problem by deleting the invalid item from the
control panel list to put the lists back in sync and the condition is
permanently gone when you save the project.
A bit scary to be deleting the item while looping but I've tested it
a bunch and don't see an issue. Would be good sometime to fix this in
the load rather than at display time.

2014-09-23

7577
 
2014-09-24
 
krueger
 
Add two more keywords to the server api test library

Run Emergent Program
Run Command Complete

Both don't just wait an arbitrary timeout for the program to complete, but
try and actually only wait as long as the command / program run.

This hopefully makes executing programs more robust, as the timeouts can be longer
without having to wait extremely long for all of the test programs to finish

7589
 
2014-09-26
 
oreilly
 
fixed issue with re-selection of tree view not setting clipboard handler -- just
had last check logic that didn't make sense given other paths to setting the 
clip handler (which has its own last check logic).  However, in doing this,
we are now emitting a SelectableHostNotifyingSignal via 
SelectableHostNotifying_impl(src_host, op) every time we re-get focus -- this
seems reasonable to me but OTOH I have no idea what this does or what the consequences

converter silently.  But I still don't know why that route causes the leak in the first
place.  need to do some more testing..

7734
 
2014-11-15
 
rohrlich
 
* Done with key binding for now. 
* The key mapping code is spread far and wide across classes and methods and the potential for breaking
things is very high so I am letting the dust settle for now.
* Here are the major changes 
- the mac "command" key is no longer interchangeable with the "control" key. Command + A is really command + A
and Control + A is really ... This is normal and provides the opportunities for shortcuts like command + F that we
couldn't have before
- with the above exception emacs mode should behave the same as before and is still the default mode though that is probably wrong
- if you don't turn on the emacs mode preferece behavior should be "standard" for your operating system though this has not been tested on Windows and only lightly on Linux
* Much of what is needed for custom key sets is in place

7760
 
2014-11-27
 
oreilly
 
* OMG that was the stupidest bug of all time!!!!!
* and it has presumably been there for a long time!  ugh.  was setting n_to_run = 0 
at a point when clearly all threads had not started -- I have no idea how this even
worked at all before.  first of all, it is completely unnecessary to reset this 
value at all, and second of all, resetting completely destroys all the subsequent
sync logic, which otherwise seemed so correct that I was really wondering where the 
bug was..
* Meanwhile, this bug probably meant that with larger numbers of threads, we werent' 
reliably engaging all of the threads in the first place.  so that would not help
our threading performance.  new results soon -- everything is now working!!

7850
 
2014-12-11
 
tkelly
 
New methods:\n * DeleteFile -- Deletes a given file from the wiki\n * GetDirectoryContents -- Fills a given data table with the names of all non-hidden, non-symlink files in the current working directory\n * FileExists -- Determines if a given file exists on the wiki\n * AddCategories -- Appends a given page on the wiki with categories pulled from a space-separated string\n * LinkFile -- Appends a given page on the wiki with a link to a single uploaded file\n * LinkFiles -- Appends a given page on the wiki with links to each of the uploaded files in a given data table\n\nChanges to existing methods:\n * PublishProject -- Made this much simpler. It now just creates/edits a page for the current project, uploads the project file, and appends a link to it on the project page. Also removed the include_hidden bool argument, as we don't want to be uploading hidden files anyway\n * UploadFile & DownloadFile -- Removed the convert_to_camel bool argument, for simplicity\n\nGeneral changes:\n * Added LOTS of comments to the code. It should be easier to understand now!\n * Misc. minor edits to improve readability & consistency

7909
 
2015-01-01
 
krueger
 
A little benchmark tool, that benchmarks the performance of the Allreduce function. 
 
Given, that the Allreduce function appears to be the bottleneck for scaling emergent to larger n with MPI, 
its performance is very critical. On the otherhand, on default settings, the standard MPI_Allreduce performance 
appears to be very problematic on a number of systems. So this lets one determine the performance under similar 
conditions as would be experienced in emergent. 
 
This also reimplements the Allreduce function in a separate class to compare a "naive" implementation to the 
standard MPI libraries. Given on a number of systems, this actually performs considerably better than the 
MPI libraries, it allows to identify how far off the tuning of the MPI libraries are from the achievable 
performance on the system.

8042
 
2015-02-28
 
oreilly
 
Major change to XCAL learning rule: now doing error-driven (medium term threshold) and
BCM self-organizing (long-term threshold) as two separate XCAL functions, and the avg_l
long-term threshold is directly computed from unit activity using new avg_l params
on the LeabraUnitSpec -- also dynamically scales amount of BCM based on level of avg_l
* no longer multiplying avg_l by su_avg_m -- it is just plain avg_l for all cons -- this
produces a much stronger contrast dynamic among the synapses, whereas before the avg_m
factor modulated each synapse to prevent weaker / off inputs from getting LTD!
* this enables BCM component to take full advantage of the full range of the XCAL
dwt function, which also helps with contrat as the "near misses" just below the
avg_l threshold are now more strongly penalized compared to the off inputs..
* also the former "s_mix" parameter is now in UnitSpec -- much more efficient than
having it in the conspec -- renamed to "m_in_s"
* overall, this is now doing a GREAT job of preventing hog units -- much better than
before!  while still preserving good overall learning, at least according to early tests.

8111
 
2015-04-02
 
rohrlich
 
* Huge speed up working with grid views with many rows in conjunction with autoscale
* The problem was that the scale range was being recalculated when the columns hadn't changed
(i.e. when the scale didn't need to be recalculated)
* So shifting rows, clicking on any checkbox in the panel, etc. - All of these caused scale code to run
* Any of these operations cost 6 seconds with the grid view we looked at yesterday for the
representational analysis and now they are instantaneous!! unless you turn on autoscale or change column view.
* Interestingly the slowdown only occurs when there are many different values. The same size matrix (48x48)
with the same 11,663 rows doesn't take anything like 6 seconds if the values are a small set of integers.
So will need to look at the code that finds the min and max as perhaps it can be sped up.
* Royal pain in the ... to find all the conditions and the best way to fix
* One of those cases where I needed to hide a member so I could test for a change of value to know how to
set the 'need_to_rescale' bool

2015-04-07
 
oreilly
 
* deep_norm is only non-zero if deep_raw is > 0 -- deep_raw is really the threshold
for all subsequent deep activity -- this means there is a default value for deep_norm
that takes effect when it is actually computed to be zero.
* This has very desirable effect of eliminating considerable dilution of the attn mask
as it propagated backward and into the TRC units -- now getting crisp signals there
* Could be key to avoiding need for synchrony of dutch guys 2012 attn model..

8224
 
2015-05-09
 
oreilly
 
* DO NOT USE!!!  NOT READY FOR RUNNING ANYTHING YET!  BUT IT DOES COMPILE OK
* complete rewrite of MTRnd to have up to 64 optimally independent random number generator
parameters, using the dcmt code from the MT folks in Japan -- each fully independent and
can be called from separate threads, but use *the same seed* to produce fully reproducible
results..
* got rid of RndSeed::GetCurrent() -- not a logical operation in parallel thread context
* RndSeed::seed is now just a single int!  that is all that is needed without GetCurrent
* takes *forever* to generate the new generator params, so these are saved in a string
and loaded from that at init time (TBD - currently generating)

8268
 
2015-05-17
 
oreilly
 
* shared connection infrastructure in place!  there's just one MAJOR problem: it only
works for the side of the connection that owns the memory -- this is the *sending*
side in Leabra, which means you can only share sending weights -- generally not
very useful.. would incur massive slowdown (and complete rewrite of code) to
make Leabra work with owned recv cons.  doh!  at least we can now make
convolutional networks in backprop..

8380
 
2015-06-25
 
oreilly
 
IMPORTANT CHANGE: all LoadData routines that take a reset_first arg now have a default
parameter of true instead of false -- the typical assumption really is that when you
load you're replacing what's already there -- load append is the special case --
having this default to false has bitten me on too many occasions, causing memory
leaks that are otherwise hard to notice (loading many repetitions of data often
doesn't affect function..)

This may break a very small number of projects, but I think it is worth it in the long
run..

8387
 
2015-06-27
 
rohrlich
 
* Fix for NULL ptrs - bug 2296
* The problem occured when updating a reference and the reference was to an object that wasn't
in the same group lineage as object being copied
* The particular case here was copying a program to another group and the program had a var reference to a DataTable in the DataTable group 
* The general solution was to see if the 'root' groups were the same and if not set null_not_found to false
in call to UpdatePointers_NewPar_Ref() so that the reference wasn't set to NULL when not found.
Previously this boolean wasn't being set and always defaulted to true.

8528
 
2015-08-21
 
oreilly
 
potential fix to locale issue: just force the damn thing to always use the "C" locale --
given that everything is based strongly on C++ code in the program system, it is not
really possible to support non-C numbers anyway (a comma means something different than a
dot in C!), so we should just go whole hog.

I briefly considered using the QString::number routines in taString but they take a
different formatting arg and it would be a fair bit of work and incompatibiltity to
switch over to using that instead.  In any case, the relevant ta_snprintf routine
is now within the .cpp file if we decide to do this at some point.

But I'm pretty sure this is the right fix.. John can you test it??

krueger
 
Add the ability to do more sophisticated parameter searches / testing.

The parameter search functionality is now a text string that takes the following syntax:

1.1;2.2;4.4:0.1:6.6;10.1:0.2:20.1

I.e. it takes a list of semi colon separated values, that either can be singular values, or can be ranges of values with a specific increment.

This implements the second part of #2364

8681
 
2015-09-27
 
rohrlich
 
* Code to support type restrictions using drag and drop
* Following the current use of 'el_base' in taList_impl I added 2 lists for acceptable and unacceptable types
that restrict subtypes of the lists 'el_base'
* These are only used for exceptions
* Types are added to these lists when an object is intialized
* For example, in Switch cases.AddAcceptableType("CaseBlock") and in Program prog_code.AddUnacceptableType("CaseBlock")
* taiMimeSource calls list->IsAcceptable(obj) which has all the logic
* Previously taiMimeSource just checked the type of el_base
* This type limiting code could be called from elsewhere but only used in drag and drop now
* So restricted 'case' to switch and 4 ProgEls that are only used in CalcLoop to CalcLoop

8685
 
2015-09-29
 
rohrlich
 
* Extend the programming drag and drop feature
* Now works to restrict	if.break and if.continue to loops
* This meant that if you had a case where you dropped a	break or continue on some ProgEl like an 'if'
the parent needed to be checked because an 'if' outside of a loop wouldn't allow a break/continue
but an 'if' in a loop should
* And there were other cases like this so the code is now recursive and if there is no definitive
answer from the immediate list IsAcceptable() is called on the parent list
* And there is a boolean on ProgEl_List 'check_with_parent' that defaults to true but for classes like
Switch we don't	 want to check with the parent

* major update of deep leabra code, to support new deep layer as a separate predictive
auto-encoder layer: removed a TON of code for computing all the deep stuff separately.
* deep.role specifies computational role of units: SUPER, DEEP, TRC -- removed separate ThalAutoEncodeUnitSpec -- SUPER is modulated by deep_mod, DEEP can send its raw act to deep_mod on SUPER, TRC has special deep plus phase.
* updated PVLV code to use new deep code: BAAcq are DEEP -- send deep_mod, and rest
are SUPER -- affected deep_mod -- for BAExt need to look at deep_lrn to support
voltage-gated dynamics.
* removed legacy lrnmod code and associated classes, which are no longer used.
* overall, removed many vars from unit class..
* lots of work needed to get PFC working again presumably, but actually should be
much cleaner with continously active deep units..
* code tested and validated on existing deep / trc auto encoder projects, and a bit on
bvpvlv.

8821
 
2015-10-29
 
krueger
 
Try and fix issue with cluster_run and extra files

The cluster run was parsing the svn update log to verify that there is a model file in the commit to run.
The regular expression however used "/models/.*", which also matches the extra files committed. As the check then verified that there is exactly one model file in the commit before running,
any extra files in the commit would result in 2 or more files matching, and thus refusing to launch the job.

I now tightended the regular expression to "/models/.*\.proj", which hopefully now only matches on the actual project file.


8822
 
2015-10-29
 
krueger
 
Actually output the error message of the exception.

We were printing the class, not the object of the exception


8823
 
2015-10-29
 
krueger
 
Try and pass through errors to emergent that happen during job submission.

This is still not ideal, because now if you submit a job and it failes to reach the job scheduer,
e.g. because one gave the wrong queue, or because the path variables are set wrong and it can't find pyqsub,
the job directly goes to the jobs_done table and never shows up in the job running.

As one is expecting the job to show up in the jobs_running table and not jobs_done table, it is quite likely
that someone still misses the fact that the job never reached the scheduler.

9117
 
2016-02-02
 
krueger
 
Add a "GetMember" command to the server protocol.

This should allow to retrieve an arbitrary member from the object tree via the server protocol.

The json command over the server protocol would be something like:
{"command": "GetProperty", "path": ".projects[\"bvPVLV\"].networks[\"bvPVLVNet\"].specs.gp[\"PVLV\"][\"PVLVLayers\"].children[\"AmygLayer\"].children[\"AmygExtLayer\"].clamp", "member": "gain"}
to retrieve the gain member from one of the layer specs.

This command should be useful for some of the testing to not need to each time write a emergent program to extract a member into a ProgVar and then use "GetVar".

It could also be useful in case one wants to create python bindings to emergent over the server protocol.

This code probably still needs some cleanup to adhere to the coding conventions or other code hygene.

9211
 
2016-02-28
 
oreilly
 
c++11 apparently has some kind of different conversion rules or something --
Strings being passed to taMisc::Choice routine from css were being deallocated
(sanitizer found it) -- Init Weights message for example caused crashing..
Only viable soln is to avoid methods that take const char*, which are very
inefficient in any case.  So, switched all those over to const String& --
seems to work..

Added NULLStr define, for empty string args --
has to be "" -- tried NULL but that goes to 0
for c++11 and activates the wrong constructor..

2016-03-02
 
oreilly
 
* so many bugs coming up with this sanitizer..  was getting a reliable crash on exit
from LayerDataEl - fixed it by getting rid of the very hacky lookup DataTableCols*
guy, which points to the data.data element, and now just do: FROM_GROUP_data.data

a list and FROM_GROUP if it is a group (previously it was always just GROUP).

9246
 
2016-03-03
 
krueger
 
Catch SVN exception when trying to create new repository.

If the cluster/username directory already exists in the svn repository, but
we didn't have a working copy checked out, emergent tried to create the directory
again in the svn repository which failed. But emergent didn't handle the case.

As we are doing a checkout after the make anyway, simply ignore the svn error on make.
If the make failed because it already exists, then great, otherwise if it failed for a
different reason, the subsequent svn checkout should fail and emergent processes that error
in a similar way as it would have previously handled the make dir exception

2016-03-10
 
krueger
 
Add a simple test for loading and saving weights.

This Runs a simple network for a while, then saves the weights, loads the weights and then saves the weights again.
The test then compares the two saved weight files to make sure the diff is empty.

This can only find cases when loading and saving weights are inconsistent, but not if they are consistent but broken.

9732
 
2016-08-05
 
oreilly
 
* several cluster run fixes to allow a running job to anticipate when it will be killed
and save weights prior to that point!
:* explicit taMisc::cluster_run setting and -cluster_run arg passed by cluster run jobs to set it -- positive id of when running a cluster job
:* ClusterRunJob -- holds all the params about a cluster run job -- cur_job static member
holds info about current job
:* has run_time_end computed run time end date
:* ClusterRun::LoadMyRunningTable -- loads local jobs_running.dat file for cr jobs, with 10 minute interval for updating already-loaded data -- could theoretically terminate rogue jobs if not in runniung table anymore, but usu that is not the failure point..
:* Network::Compute_Weights checks for running dat info and saves weights if going to
be terminated within 5 minutes!
:* cluster run script now automatically does a "check running jobs" every 10 mins.  very low overhead and useful so you can monitor others' jobs etc.  and running job can monitor itself..
:* added pub_cite field to taProject -- citation for publication associated with project -- will add to media wiki template.  already uploads it.  need to add to dialog.
* NONE OF THE ABOVE HAS BEEN TESTED!  just first pass impl.  shouldn't break anything.. :)

9859
 
2016-08-18
 
oreilly
 
* spent whole day debugging ANOTHER annoying but at least 100% reliable crash when
deleting layer groups in cecn/ccn_ed3/chapter_10/sir.proj -- good news is that I was
able to fix it!!  2 key things, in ISelectableHost.cpp:
* CloseLater instead of Close on the object
* taMisc::ProcessEvents after undo save
* Either of these alone was not enough!  now able to do 100% reliable sequential deletes
on layers and layer groups, no problemo!
* Meanwhile, fixed some update-triggering stuff during Layer and Projection CutLinks() that
I thought might be the problem (but weren't, but are good to do anyway).
* STILL had a crash bug on delete of MatrixLayer -- in a ControlPanel viewing its del_inhib
member -- after trying a bunch of things here, turned out that due to a slew of errors
during loading, somehow the UAE is not called during loading, so the bases were not
getting registered.  Ugh.  Not going to fix this one today.  Definitely works fine
for normal case, so it is something about having tons of errors.  And MOST of the control panels are still getting updated.  NO idea why last two are not.
* Meanwhile, fixed up a lot of the base handling stuff, and better optimized (and renamed)
the updt_while_running flag.  Wasn't adding method bases!  so if you deleted an obj
whose methods you were using in control panel, it would crash.  reason was the updating --
fixed that instead..
* added repaint() calls in iConsole -- get instant updates of console without going
through event system -- very nice for debugging etc.

9892
 
2016-08-21
 
krueger
 
Don't output the entire diff for the random weight initialisation test

As the weights file is very large in this test, outputting the full diff, if the random seeds are not identical, is very slow and chokes jenkins,
So use the -q flag on the diff to only output if there is a difference or not.
